<section type="title-page">
A most excellent and
LEARNED WOORKE OF CHI&#173;
rurgerie, called Chirurgia parua Lanfranci,
Lanfranke of Mylayne his briefe: reduced from dyuers
translations to our vulgar or vsuall frase,
and now first published in the En&#173;
glyshe prynte by Iohn Halle
Chirurgien. 
Who hath thervnto neces&#173;
sarily annexed. 

A Table, as wel of the names of diseases and simples
with their vertures, as also of all other termes of the
arte opened. Very profitable for the better vn&#173;
derstanding of the same, or other
like workes. 

And in the ende a compendious worke of Anatomie, more 
vtile and profitable, then any here tofore in the
Englyshe tongue publyshed. 

AN HISTORIALL EXPOSTULATION
also against the beastly abusers, both of Chy&#173;
rurgerie and Phisicke in our tyme: With a 
goodly doctrine, and instruction, ne&#173;
cessary to be marked and 
folowed of all true 
Chirurgi<expan type="">en</expan>s. 
All these faithfully gathered, and diligently s<damage>et</damage>
forth, by the sayde Iohn Halle. 

Imprinted at London in Flete streate, nyghe
unto saint Dunstones churche,
by Thomas Marshe. 
<term lang="la">AN.</term> 1565. 
</section>



</page>

<page no="1">
<section type="Glossary">
<heading>Here beginneth
the Interpretiue Table vpon 
Lanfranke hys worke. </heading>

<wordgroup1 type="a" object="A">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Abrotonum. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="southernwood(n)" lexeme="word(n)" lexeme="wood(a)">SOthernwode, is called in Greke
<term lang="gk">&#x0391;&#x03B2;&#x03C1;&#x03CC;&#x03C4;&#x03BF;&#x03BD;&#x03BF;&#x03BD;</term>, and in Latine <term lang="la">Abrotonum</term>,
wherof there are two kyndes, the 
male and the female: but that which
groweth wyth vs is the male. And
is (after Galen) whotte and drye in
the thirde degre: hauinge a certaine 
digestiue, and incisiue power, more
then Wormwode: but hathe some sharpnesse, as hathe
Wormwode and also bitternesse: And therfore kylleth
Wormes, and is an ennemye to the stomacke, as is Scri&#173;
phium. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Abrotonon</term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">De symplici&#173;
um medica&#173;
mentorum fa<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
cultitatibus. 
libro. 6. </term></note>
</wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Absinthium. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="wormwood(n)" lexeme="sea wormwood(n)" lexeme="Pontic wormwood(n)" lexeme="Roman wormwood(n)" lexeme="wormwood gentle(n)" lexeme="French wormwood(n)" lexeme="(en)gentle wormwood(n)">OF Wormwode (called in Latine <term lang="la">Absinthium</term>, and
in Greke <term lang="gk">&#x0391;&#x03C8;&#x03AF;&#x03BD;&#x03B8;&#x03B9;&#x03BF;&#x03BD;</term>,) there are . iii. kindes, (beside <expan type="">the</expan>
common stinkinge Wormwode, wyth broade
leaues called <term lang="la">Absinthium rusticum</term>. ) The fyrste is
called <term lang="la">Seriphium</term>, and <term lang="la">Marinum</term>, in Englishe sea Wormwode, 
and groweth plentiously in Kente, by the sea bankes, and
salte marishes. The seconde is called of Dioscorides <term lang="la">Absinthi&#173;
um Ponticum</term>, of Mesues <term lang="la">Romanum</term>, and in Englishe pontike,
or Romane Wormwode, or Wormewode Gentille, in Es&#173;
sexe Cipers: and groweth now in diuers gardines of Lon&#173;



</page>

<page no="2">
don, Kent, and Essexe. The thirde is <term lang="la">Santonicum</term>, so called of 
Santonis, (a region in France named nowe <term lang="fr">Xantongue</term>,) and 
therfore in Englishe not vnaptlye Frenche Wormwode. 
The best of these to be put in inward medicines, is the <term lang="en">P<expan type="">on</expan>&#173;
tike</term> or <term lang="en">Romane Wormwode</term>: neither oughte anye other 
kinde to be vsed in steade therof: thoughe none of them be 
wythoute their singuler vertues. Pontike Wormwode,
(saith Galen) is lesse whot then all the rest, hauing muche
adstriction, but no lesse drying. <term lang="la">Santonic<expan type="">um</expan></term> is next in faculties, 
but somwhat weaker then <term lang="la">Seriphio</term>: in heating, drying, and
extenuation. <term lang="la">Seriphium</term> is colder then <term lang="la">Abrotono</term>, but whotter
then <term lang="la">Pontico</term>, and enemy to the stomacke: for that it hathe
(with hys bitternesse:) a certeyn saltnesse, and also some ad&#173;
striction, thoughe but litle: so are also <term lang="la">Abrotonum</term>, and <term lang="la">Santoni&#173;
cum</term>: onlye <term lang="la">Ponticum</term> is acceptable to the stomacke, and of t<expan type="">em</expan>&#173;
perament whot in the first degre, and dry in the thirde. </xpln> 
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Apsinthion</term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Absinthi<expan type="">um</expan> ru&#173;
sticum</term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Absinthi<expan type="">um</expan> Se&#173;
riphium, uel marinum</term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Absinthium
Pontic<expan type="">um</expan>, uel Romanum</term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Absinthium
Santonicum</term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">De sym. med. 
facul. li. 6. </term></note>

</wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="acacia(n)">Acacia. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="sloe(n)" lexeme="gum arabic(n)" >MEn vse c<expan type="">om</expan>monly the iuyce of Sloes for Acacia, which
is not so: for Acacia is a thorny tre, growing in Egipt,
hauinge whyte sedes closed in coddes, wherowte is
pressed a iuyce: whiche beinge dryed is occupied in medi&#173;
cines, vnder this name Acacia. It dryeth after Galen in <expan type="">the</expan>
thirde degree, and cooleth (being washed) in the second: but 
vnwashed in the firste, (for by washinge it loseth his sharp&#173;
nesse:) and is of an earthly substance, hauing therwith wa&#173;
tery, and also whotte and thin partes. Where it is layde, it
leaueth the place dryed &#38;  contracted. The gumme of thys
tree is the true gumme Arabike. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">De sym. med. 
facul. li. 6. </term></note>
</wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="acanthus(n)">Acanthus. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="bear(n)" lexeme="breech(n)" lexeme="bear's foot(n)" lexeme="brank-ursine(n)"><term lang="la">BRanca Vrsina</term>: (whiche is called in Greke <term lang="gk">&#x03AC;&#x03BA;&#x03B1;&#x03BD;&#x03B4;&#x03B1;</term>, in la&#173;
tine Acanthus, and <term lang="la">P&#230;derota</term>,) is called in English beares 
breche, and no beares foote, as some abusiuely bothe 



</page>

<page no="3">
saye and vse, despysinge suche as woulde reforme their ac&#173;
customed error. Dioscorides appoynteth to <term lang="la">Acantho</term> leaues
lyke letuce, but larger, longer, and indented as <term lang="la">Eruca</term>: wher
by it is euident, that it can not be bearefote. 
Beares breche groweth in gardines, the leaues wherof
(saithe Galen) obteine a moderate digestinge faculty. The
roote is desiccatiue, and lightly incisiue, consisting of thin or
t<expan type="">en</expan>der partes, and is one of the . iiii. principal mollificatiues. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Li. 6. de sym. 
medi. facul. </term></note>
</wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Accidentia. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="withfall(n)"><term lang="la">Accidens</term> generally, betokeneth thinges chauncing, or
belonging to substances, whiche they maye haue or
lacke, wythout corruption of the same. But <term lang="la">accid<expan type="">en</expan>t<emend err="">e</emend>s</term>
are Phisicallye of Galen thus defined, in the ende of hys firste boke. <term lang="la">De methodo medendi</term>. 
Those thinges, that doe necessarilye folowe that consti&#173;
tution, from whence groweth and action: in vs being whole 
are named <term lang="la">Accidentia</term>: but if we be sicke <term lang="gk">&#x03A3;&#x03CD;&#x03BC;&#x03C0;&#x03C4;&#x03C9;&#x03BC;&#x03B1;&#x03C4;&#x03B1;</term>. Yet
are <term lang="la">accidentes</term> notes also of griefes, after his mynde, <term lang="la">li. i. de
locis affectis</term>, sayinge. <term lang="la">Ex propriis accidentibus etiam innotescit af&#173;
fectus locus: nam ore Ventriculi affecto, fastidium infestat</term>. That is
a place affected is knowen by hys proper accidentes: as the 
mouth of the stomacke affected, lothsomnesse infesteth the 
same. And these are termed of oure Englishe Phisike wry&#173;
ters, wythfalles. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Symptomata</term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="gk">&#x03C3;&#x03CD;&#x03BC;&#x03C0;&#x03C4;&#x03B1;&#x03BC;&#x03B1;</term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">id est incursus
concursus, uel
casus. </term></note>
</wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="acetum(n)">Acetum. </form> 
<xpln lang="en">CAlled in Greke <term lang="gk">&#x039F;&#x03BE;<expan type="">&#x03BF;&#x03C2;</expan></term>, consisteth of substances, bothe
whotte and colde, and they bothe of tender partes,
(wherin yet colde hathe the masterye,) and dryeth
in the thyrde degree, and hathe Repercussyue, Tenua&#173;
tynge, and discussyue vertues. But yet dyffereth it in fa&#173;
cultyes, accordynge to the temperamente of the Wyne 



</page>

<page no="4">
wherof it is made. As if it be made of smalle wynes, it co&#173;
leth effectuallye inflammations, and repelleth whotte co&#173;
lerike swellinges, as in <term lang="la">Oxicrato</term>. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Oxos</term>. </note>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="acorus(n)">Acorus. </form> 
<xpln lang="en">WHiche the Grecians calle <term lang="gk">&#x1F04;&#x03BA;&#x03BF;&#x03C1;&#x03BF;&#x03BD;</term>, hathe a roote
somewhat bitter, and of pleasante odour, and is
whotte and drye in the thirde degree, and of sub&#173;

the hardnesse of the panicle Ceratocides: whervnto <expan type="">the</expan> iuyce
serueth best. And because it is thoughte not to growe with
vs, we maye after the myndes of some, substitute for it <term lang="la">Ca&#173;
lamum odor<expan type="">an</expan>tum</term> or as Galen willeth, <term lang="la">Radicem Asari</term>. For truly
they erre verye muche, that vse <term lang="la">Gladiolo luteo</term> for <term lang="la">Acoro</term>. But
Doctor Turner taketh rather <term lang="la">Gal<emend err="i">a</emend>ngam maiorem</term> for dyuers
reasons to be <term lang="la">Acorum</term>, then <term lang="la">Calamum aromaticum</term>, as dyuers
have thoughte. </xpln>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="adeps(n)">Adeps. </form> 
<xpln lang="en">FOr <expan type="">the</expan> better vnderst<expan type="">an</expan>ding of these words Adeps, <term lang="la">Seuum</term>,
<term lang="la">Axungia</term>, (called in Greke <term lang="gk">&#x039F;&#x03BE;&#x03CD;&#x03B3;&#x03B3;&#x03B9;&#x03BF;&#x03BD;</term>) and <term lang="la">Pinguedo</term>, (na&#173;
med in Greke <term lang="gk">&#x03A0;&#x03B9;&#x03BC;&#x03B5;&#x03BB;&#x03B7;</term>) and their differ<expan type="">en</expan>ces: I refferre
you to my Anatomye a place for that moste mete. All the
whiche are in compositions of medicines (thoughe the In&#173;
terpretors of Galen doe muche frequente thys woorde
adeps,) wythout precise difference vsed for suche greases, su&#173;
ets, or fattines as are tried from the bodyes of beastes. &#38;c. 
Of the whiche <term lang="la">Adeps Leoninus</term>, (saithe Galen) dothe moste
valientlye as well heate as digeste. Wherunto <term lang="la">adeps pardi</term>:
hathe the nexte place, whiche mollifyeth moderatly. The
power of <term lang="la">adeps anserinus</term>, is lesse heatynge and digestynge,
but somewhat more mollifyinge, and consisteth of subtille
partes, as dothe the fatte of all byndes. A little differynge



</page>

<page no="5">
from this is <term lang="la">adeps gal<emend err="">l</emend>inaceus</term>, consistinge as in a meane: and
is a moste familiar medicyne for infl<expan type="">am</expan>mations. <term lang="la">Adeps Suil&#173;
lus</term>, is of all other fattes, the softest, moystest and weakest
and therefore is conueniente for tender bodyes. How <term lang="la">Adeps
Capran<expan type="">um</expan></term>, &#38;  <term lang="la">Boum</term>: how much the str<expan type="">on</expan>ger they are, then <term lang="la">adeps
porci</term>: so muche the more fyttlye agree they, wyth bodyes
of harder, or str<expan type="">on</expan>ger nature, &#38;  vnto scirhous hardnesses. &#38;c. 
The fattes morouer of masculyne beastes are alwaies the
whotter and dryer: of the female contrarye, and of <expan type="">the</expan> male
gelded, it is euer like to that of the female. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Oxyngion</term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Seuum</term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Pimele</term>. </note>

5. et. 11. de

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Adustio. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="adust(a)" lexeme="adustion(n)">ADustion, is as well the burnynge of medicynes,
by materialle fire, as of humores in the body,
by the excessiue distemperature, of potencialle
heate therin: Wherof they are called aduste, or
burned humores. </xpln>
</wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Agresta. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="sorrel(n)" lexeme="verjuice(n)">ALthoughe <term lang="la">Agresta</term> whiche the Grecians calle <term lang="gk">&#x03CC;&#x03BC;&#x03C6;&#x1F70;&#173;
&#x03BA;&#x03B9;&#x03BF;&#x03BD;</term>: be properlye the liquor of vnripe grapes, pres&#173;
sed oute, (whiche some haue ignorantly interpreted
the iuyce of Sorell. ) I thinke the iuyce of Crabbes, whiche
we calle comm<expan type="">on</expan>ly veriuce, may be safely, or without great
error, vsed for Agresta. And that the rather, because <term lang="la">Lanfran&#173;
cus</term> in the cure of <term lang="la">Carbunculi</term>. Willeth <term lang="la">sunnum pomorum Agre&#173;
stium</term>, to be taken in suche sorte as be often before had done
<term lang="la">Agrestam</term>. 

Veriuce is of colde and drye facultye, whereby it aswa&#173;
geth and represseth the inflammations of ardent humors,
and sharpe, wherby it cutteth and thinneth grosse, &#38;  tough
Phlegme. And is muche praised, in comforting the weak&#173;
nes of the hart, and in swounding. The Crabbe tree is na&#173;
med in Latine <term lang="la">Malus syluestris</term>. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Omphacton</term></note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Latine etiam
Omphacium. </term></note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Malus sylue&#173;
stris</term></note>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="aloe(n)">Aloe. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="sea(n)" lexeme="ay-green(n)">ALoe is commonly numbered (am<expan type="">on</expan>g wryters) of two
kyndes only, although ther be found amonge the A&#173;
pothecaries in c<expan type="">om</expan>mon practice thre sortes to be sold:
namely, <term lang="la">Succotrina</term>, <term lang="la">Hepatica</term>, &#38;  <term lang="la">Cabalina</term>. But who so readeth
<term lang="la">Dioscoridem</term>, and other auncient wryters, shall perceiue that
they knewe but of two sortes, as one fyne and pure, which
some calle <term lang="la">Aloen Hepaticam</term>. The other, which (because it is
full of drosse and sande) semeth to be the bothome or refuse
of the pure iuyce, they name <term lang="la">Aloen Cabalinan</term>, because (as I
suppose) it not beinge mete for man his bodye, was only u&#173;
sed to heale the diseases of horses. But of <expan type="">the</expan> purest I iudge
there is none other difference, but that the same whyche
one author calleth <term lang="la">Hepaticam</term>, an other calleth <term lang="la">Succotrinam</term>,
whiche also moued <term lang="la">Iacobus Syluius</term> to reporte that Dioscorides
and <term lang="la">Haliabbus</term> praise <term lang="la">Aloen Hepatican</term>: but Auicenna and Mesues
<term lang="la">Aloen Succotrinam</term>. It is the iuyce of an herb, called in Greke
<term lang="gk">&#x1F02;&#x03BB;&#x03BF;&#x03AE;</term> and in Latine <term lang="la">Semper Viuum Marinum</term>: In English herbe
Aloes or Sea Aigren: whose iuice is brought to vs fr<expan type="">om</expan> India
(for ther groweth the best,) is a proffitable medicin for ma&#173;
ny thinges, through the drying that it hathe, without cor&#173;
rosion. It bindeth moderatlye, but is verye bitter, and ther
fore loseth the belly. It drieth in the thirde degre, &#38;  heateth
stronglye in the first, or lightlye in the second: and is grate&#173;
full to the stomacke. It glueth together holowe places, and
healeth vlcers hard to be cured: <term lang="la">Maxime qu&#230; in ano &#38;  puden&#173;
dis sunt</term>, and stieped in water, healpeth the inflammatyons
in them, and also in the mouthe and Eyes. In summe,



</page>

<page no="8">
It repelleth, digesteth, and so gently scoureth: that it hur&#173;
teth not cleane sores. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Aloe Succorri<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
na</term></note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Aloe Hepati&#173;
ca. </term></note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Aloe Cabalina</term></note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Galenus, de
sym. med. li. 6</term></note>
</wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="althea(n)">Alth&#230;a</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="hollyhock(n)" lexeme="marshmallow(n)">WHiche hathe bene of longe time taken, (not with
out manifest error,) for Holihocke: is called in 
Greke <term lang="gk">&#x03B1;&#x03BB;&#x03B4;&#x03B1;&#x03B9;&#x03B1;, &#x03BA;&#x03B1;&#x03B9; &#x0399;&#x03B2;&#x03AF;&#x03C3;&#x03BA;&#x03BF;&#x03C2;</term>, in Latine <term lang="la">Alth&#230;a</term>, and
<term lang="la">Ibiscus</term>, of the Apothecaries Bismalua, and <term lang="la">Maluauis&#173;

It discusseth, digesteth, breaketh, and Cicatrizeth, as
saithe Dioscorides, and hathe power (sayeth Galen,) to digeste,
lose, and take awaye inflammations: to mitigate also, and
concoct. But the roote, and the sede are of t<expan type="">en</expan>derer partes,
and shewe a more dryinge, and scouringe vertue. </xpln>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="alumen(n)">Alumen. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="alum(n)">OF Alum, (called in Greke <term lang="gk">&#x03C3;&#x03C4;&#x03C5;&#x03C0;&#x03C4;&#x03B7;&#x03C1;&#x03AF; &#x03B1;</term>,) saythe Diosco&#173;
rides, there are manye kindes. But for the vse of
medicine, <term lang="la">Alumen Scissile</term>, or <term lang="la">Fissile</term>, called <term lang="gk">&#x03C3;&#x03C4;&#x03C5;&#x03C0;&#x03B7;&#x03C4;&#x03C1;&#x03AF;&#x03B1;
&#x03C3;&#x03C7;&#x03B9;&#x03C7;&#x1F74;</term>, <term lang="la">Alumen Rotundum</term> called therfore <term lang="gk">&#x03C3;&#x03C4;&#x03C1;&#x03BF;&#x03B3;&#x03B3;&#x03CD;&#x03BB;&#x03B7;</term>, and <term lang="gk">&#x03B0;&#x03B3;&#x03C1;&#x03B1;</term>
<term lang="la">hoc est Liquidum, uel Humidum</term>: are saythe he, moste bled. Prai&#173;
singe also amonge them <term lang="la">Fissile</term> for the best. 
<term lang="la">Alumen</term> (saythe Galen,) dothe in all hys kindes vehemently
binde and are al of grosse partes, but the subtillest of all the
rest is <term lang="la">alumen fissile, uel scission</term>, next unto it is <term lang="la">Alumen Rotond<expan type="">um</expan></term>
and <term lang="gkt">Astragaloton</term>: but <term lang="gk">&#x03C0;&#x03BB;&#x03B1;&#x03BA;&#x03AF;&#x03C4;&#x03B9;&#x03C2;</term> <term lang="la">id est crustarum</term>, <term lang="gk">&#x03C0;&#x03BB;&#x03B9;&#x03BD;&#x03B8;&#x03AF;&#x03C4;&#x03B9;&#x03C2;</term>, <term lang="la">hoc est 
latercularium</term>, because it is like brickes or fyles, and <term lang="la">alumen

<term lang="gk">&#x03C0;&#x03B1;&#x03C1;&#x03AC;&#x03C6;&#x03BF;&#x03C1;&#x03BF;&#x03C2;</term>, <term lang="la">hoc est Scabrum</term>, as it were perverted, or wyth
soyle adulterate. And <term lang="gk">&#x03C4;&#x03C1;&#x03B9;&#x03C7;&#x03AF;&#x03C4;&#x03B7;&#x03C2;</term> <term lang="la">quasi Capillare</term>, for that it is

his corrosiues,) <term lang="la">Alumen Saccharinunt, Alumen Vitreum, &#38;c. 



</page>

<page no="9">

alle,) is a vaine of the earthe, wherof there is founde in I&#173;
talye great plentye, in the manner of a rock. And is saythe
Discorides, of heatinge, binding, and purging facultye. Be&#173;

dum</term>, saythe <term lang="la">Brasauolus</term>, is called also <term lang="la">Alumen Roch&#230;</term>: who also

<xpln lang="en" lexeme="ambulation(n)">AMbulation is the wanderinge, or goinge aboute of

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Amphemerina Febris. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="interpolation(n)" lexeme="phlegm(n)" >SO vnderstand I Lanfranke, by <term lang="la">Anfimerina</term>, as I fynde

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="amygdala(n)">Amygdala. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="sweet almond(n)" lexeme="almond(n)">IN Greke <term lang="gk">&#x03B1;&#x03BC;&#x03C5;&#x03B3;&#x03B4;&#x03AC;&#x03BB;&#x03B7;</term>. Of Almondes, that sort whiche for

also helpe the paines of the side, of the splene, of Colon, &#38;  of
the reynes, comming of the same. Howbeit they moue not
the bely, neither doe they nourishe muche. The swete Al&#173;
mondes, thoughe (in the vertues abouesayde) the weaker:
yet are they moderatly whot, &#38;  mete for meates. They al&#173;
so moue vrine, and amend the moist vices of the stomacke. </xpln>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Amylum</form> 
<xpln lang="en">WHich we corruptly calle <term lang="la">Amidum</term>: is that which <expan type="">the</expan> Gre&#173;
cians haue auncientlye called <term lang="gkt">Amelon</term>, and is nothinge
else, but the milke or iuyce, of wheate certaine daies steped
in water, and then pressed oute, whiche for his myldnes, is
vsually put in Collyries, as a moste apte medicyne for ma&#173;
ladyes of the eies. For beinge exactlye washed, it hath saith
Galen, neither sharpnesse, nor adstriction: neyther heating
nor coolinge. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">De com. med. 
ii. loca,lib. 4. </term></note>
</wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="anacard(n)">Anacardus. </form> 
<xpln lang="en">OR after Ruellius <term lang="la">anacardi<expan type="">um</expan></term>: is the frute of a tre, growing
in <term lang="la">Sicilia</term>, and <term lang="la">Apulia</term>, called vulgarly, <term lang="la">Pediculus Elephantis</term>. 
The iuyce wherof is called <term lang="la">Mel Anacardi</term>: which is a ruptory
medicine. <term lang="la">Anacardi<expan type="">um</expan></term> (saith <term lang="la">Ruellius</term>) of <expan type="">the</expan> later Grecians, (for <expan type="">the</expan> 
a<expan type="">un</expan>cients make therof no m<expan type="">en</expan>tion,) is a familiar tre among
the Indians, &#38;  groweth also in the hilles of Sicilia, <expan type="">the</expan> throwe
out flames of fire: wyth a frute like a birdes harte, (wherof
it is thoughte to haue his name,) hauinge therin a redde or
bloudy iuyce, whiche floweth oute lyke bloude. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Pediculus Ele&#173;
phantis. </term></note>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="anatomy(n)">Anatomia. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="dissection(n)"><term lang="gk">&#x0391;&#x03BD;&#x03B1;&#x03C4;&#x03BF;&#x03BC;&#x1F74;</term> is the dissection or cutting vp of man his body,
or the bodyes of beastes: wherby knowledge may be attai&#173;
ned, by discerning, and considering the partes therof, with
their formes, offices, processes, and colligations, one wyth
another: Wherby certeintye is hadde, as wel howe ware&#173;
ly to worke, as wiselye to Prognosticate. </xpln>

vnwashed) a mighty adstriction, which by washing is made
wel nere vtterly wythout biting, it is necessarily vsed with
medicines for the eies, &#38;  for his vertues therin, obteined to
be called <term lang="gk">&#x03C0;&#x03BB;&#x03B1;&#x03C4;&#x03C5;&#x03BF;&#x03C6;&#x03B8;&#x03B1;&#x03BB;&#x03BC;&#x03CC;&#x03BD;</term>, because it openeth the eyes. </xpln>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="anthrax(n)">Anthrax. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="carbuncle(n)" lexeme="adust(n)" lexeme="adustion(n)">ALthough many haue ignor<expan type="">an</expan>tly deuided <term lang="la">Anthrac<expan type="">em</expan></term>, from
<term lang="la">Carbunculo</term>: as though they were sondry and seueral tu&#173;
mores: it is moste euident that it is one thinge: &#38;  that
<term lang="gk">&#x1F04;&#x03BD;&#x03B8;&#x03C1;&#x03B1;&#x03B6;</term>, is the same in greke, wherof <term lang="la">Carbunculus</term>, is <expan type="">the</expan> name
in Latyne and signifyeth a burnyng cole, whyche thys tu&#173;
more dothe verye muche resemble (in the augmentation,)
bothe in colour and nature, hauing also in the declination a
blacke crustous eschare, made by adustion, representinge a
quenched cole, whiche euidentlye sheweth, howe excessyue
heat, ioyned for the moste part wyth venemous matter, is
cause of this tumore. 



</page>

<page no="12">
Yet is it notwythstandynge deuided into kyndes: wherof
the greatest and most dangerous sort, appeareth common&#173;
lye in the time of Pestilente infection: and consysteth (as 
saythe Galen,) of melancholye aduste. The other sort (beinge
not so fearfulle, and comminge at other tymes,) is made of 
whotte boylinge or burned bloude: whiche semeth to be
made, or turned into Melancholy, or as he sayth in an other
place, of whotte bloude, turned by adustion into the nature
of Melancholye. And surelye thus is Lanfrancus, and other
wryters of his time to be vnderstanded, when they speake
of <term lang="la">Anthrax</term> or <term lang="la">Carbunculus</term>, for so shall they in the reste agree
with Galen, and other aunciente wryters. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Carbunculus</term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">In lib. de tumo
ribus pr&#230;ter
naturam. </term></note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">In lib. de diffe&#173;
rentiis Febri&#173;
um. Cap. iii. </term></note>
</wordentry>

the aunciente
and most ler&#173;
ned wryters. </note>

Risus &#38;  
H&#230;morhoidum</term>. </form>

Petrapium</term>. Stone Persley. </subxpln>



</page>

<page no="13">
<subform lang="gk">&#x1F34;&#x03C0;&#x03C0;&#x03BF;&#x03C3;&#x03AD;&#x03BB;&#x03B9;&#x03BD;&#x03BF;&#x03BD;</subform> <subxpln lang="en"> <term lang="la">Apium equinum. 
Equapium siue. 
Olus atrum</term>. Alexanders, or
greate Persley. 
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Hipposelinon</term></note>
</subxpln>

<subform lang="gk">&#x03C3;&#x03AD;&#x03BB;&#x03B9;&#x03BD;&#x03BF;&#x03BD; &#x03A6;&#x03C1;&#x03B1;&#x03B3;&#173;
&#x03BC;&#x03CA;&#x03C4;&#x03C5;&#x03B6;</subform> <subxpln lang="en"> <term lang="la">Apium sepis, uel
Apium sepiculare</term>. Hedge Persley. 
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Selinon
Phragmites</term>. </note>
</subxpln>

And whersoeuer thou fyndest anye kinde of <term lang="la">Apium</term>, disa&#173;
greinge, (whether in sense or Interpretati<expan type="">on</expan>) to this order,
holde it for false. 

<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Batrachion</term>. </note>
As for <term lang="la">Apium H&#230;morrhoidum</term>, and <term lang="la">Apium Risus</term>: It is but an
abuse and confusion, to reckon them emonge the kindes of
<term lang="la">Apium</term>: amonge whome, (either in forme or faculties,) they
can haue no place. But are kyndes of <term lang="la">Ranunculus</term>, called in 
Greke <term lang="gk">&#x03B2;&#x03B1;&#x03C4;&#x03C1;&#x03AC;&#x03C7;&#x03B9;&#x03BF;&#x03BD;</term>, in English Crowfote, and Frogmarche
wherof also ther are very manye kindes, and all of whotte
and blistering property: wherof loke more in <term lang="la">Flamula</term>. 

<note type="m"><term lang="la">De sym. med. 
fac. li. 8. </term></note>
<term lang="la">Apium</term> saythe Galen, is so whotte: <term lang="la">Vt Vrinam &#38;  menses cieat</term>. 
It breaketh wynde, but that dothe the sede, more then the
herbe, and is to the mouthe of the stomacke moste accepta&#173;
ble. The seade of <term lang="la">Oreoselinum</term>, and <term lang="la">Hipposelinum</term>, are of lyke
vertues, but <term lang="la">Oreoselinum</term> is the stronger, hitherto Galen. <term lang="la">Api&#173;
um</term> is whotte in the seconde degre, and dry in the middes of
the thirde. </xpln>
<lemenote>
"Frogmarche" is not found in the OED but must be a variant of "march," n. 1 ("Wild celery, <i>Apium graveolens</i>"). 
</lemenote>
</wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apostema. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="tumor(n)" lexeme="apostem(n)">AS <term lang="gk">&#x03B1;&#x03C0;&#x03BF;&#x03C2;&#x03B7;&#x03BC;&#x03B1;</term>. <term lang="la">Hoc est Spatium, siue interuallum</term>, whyche
signifyeth distance or space, is the same whyche the
Latines caule <term lang="la">Abscessum</term>, of <term lang="la">Abscedo</term>. And Galen calleth
it <term lang="la">Particularum diductionem</term>, and are certyne dispositions,
wherin suche bodyes as before touched together, are nowe
differente, and seuered one from an other. Wherof (saythe
Galen,) there must nedes be made a void space, conteining
some substance, eyther flatuous, or moyste, or compound of
bothe. Whiche (if it hange, or tarye longe therin,) receiueth
divers alterations. Wherof the greater, is usuallye called



</page>

<page no="14">
<term lang="la">Apostema</term>, and the lesse <term lang="la">Pustula</term>. So is for <term lang="la">Exitura</term>, in L<expan type="">an</expan>franke
and others of that age, and also of a <term lang="la">Avicenna</term>, to be vnderst<expan type="">an</expan>&#173;
ded <term lang="la">Tumor suppuratus</term>: that is a suppurate aposteme, or riped
tumore. But of these I nede here make the lesse declarati&#173;
on, for so much as matter Gale, hathe so worthilye, and
most exquisitly in his Institution of a Chirurgien, opened
these thinges at large. Where thou maist, bothe in thys &#38;
many other maters, be right sufficiently satisfied. </xpln>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="aqua(n)">Aqua. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="water(n)">WAter is of temperament cold, contrarye to fier and of
all other thinges (saithe Galen) the moistest: and that,
as it is vtterly without qualities, (as wythoute taste, with&#173;
out sauor, and moste cleare,) so is it moste pure: And as it
b<expan type="">en</expan>deth from this, so receiueth it qualities, to heat or coole,
according to the thinges, therwith mixed. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">lib. 1. de com&#173;
positione me&#173;
dicamentor<expan type="">um</expan>
&#38; lib. 2. de
symp. med. fa
cul. ca. 8 &#38;  . 5</term></note>
</wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="Aristolochia(n)">Aristolochia. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="birthwort(n)" lexeme="hollowwort(n)" lexeme="clematite(n)"><term lang="gk">&#x0391;&#x03C1;&#x03B9;<expan type="">&#x03C3;&#x03C4;</expan>&#x03BF;&#x03BB;&#x03CC;&#x03C7;&#x03B9;&#x03B1;</term> is of . iii. kindes, as Dioscorides saith: &#38;  obteineth
that name, of the precious helpe that women receiue ther
by, in their hard labours of children: which doctor Turner
hathe therfore moste aptly called in English Birthworte. 
The first is called <term lang="la">Aristolochia rotunda</term>. The second <term lang="la">Aristolochia
longa</term>. The thirde <term lang="la">Clematitis</term>: bisyde these <term lang="la">Plinius</term> addeth a 
fourthe kinde, called <term lang="gk">&#x03C0;&#x03B9;&#x03C0;<expan type="">&#x03C3;&#x03C4;</expan>&#x03C1;&#x03B9;&#x03C3;&#x03BF;&#x03BB;&#x03CC;&#x03C7;&#x03B9;&#x03B1;</term>. 

The Apothecaries haue of longe time erred, in sellinge
Holoworte for <term lang="la">Aristolochia rotunda</term>: but some of late haue in
the selues reformed this euel, &#38;  doe sel the true thing. But
surely many women &#38;  midwiues do erre muche more gre&#173;
uously in my iudgment, who pl<expan type="">an</expan>t in their gardens, a use in
womens labours. <term lang="la">Bistorta</term> in the stead of <term lang="la">Aristolochia</term> calling
it <term lang="la">Astrologia</term>: whyche is of a coolynge and verye astringente
nature, &#38;  therfore causeth rather retention, th<expan type="">en</expan> expulsion:
I aduertise all good women therfore, that are willynge to
helpe them selues and others, to seke for the true thynge,
whiche thy maye be sure to obteine, by the aduise of some



</page>

<page no="15">
learned Phisicien, or experte Chirurgien, at the trustye A&#173;
pothecaries hand. It groweth plentiouslye in Italye, and
<term lang="la">Aristolochia longa</term>, or at leaste <term lang="la">Clematitis</term>: groweth nowe
in diuerse gardens in Englande, as in London: in a gar&#173;
den of master Holande, late Chirurgien to the Quenes
highnesse: of whome I had rotes, whiche growe nowe in
my gard<expan type="">en</expan> at Maidstone. Of <term lang="la">Aristolochia</term> and his kindes, read
more in master Turners Herballe. And for <term lang="la">Bistorta</term> reade
<term lang="la">Fuchsius, de historia Stirpium</term>. The rote saythe Galen is bitter
and somewhat sharpe, but the rounde is the subtillest. Of 
the other. ii. <term lang="la">Clematitis</term> smelleth swetest, but yet is the wea&#173;
ker. The longe is so subtille as the rounde, and hathe hea&#173;
tinge, and scouringe power, degesting, and scouring away,
lesse then the rounde: but heateth rather more then lesse. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Pistolochia</term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Bistorta</term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Galenus de symplicibus
lib. 6. </term></note>
</wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="borax(n)">Baurach. </form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="borax(n)" lexeme="nitrum(n)">Whether it weare the mynde of Lanfrancus, or of some

of Nitrum. It is by the testemonies of Galen and Mesues: of
the facultye and nature of Nitrum, thoughe somewhat wea&#173;

<xpln lang="en"><term lang="gk">&#x0392;&#x03B4;&#x1F72;&#x03BB;&#x03BB;&#x03B9;&#x03BF;&#x03BD;</term>, whiche (as saith Dioscorides) some calle <term lang="gk">&#x03B2;&#x03CC;&#x03BB;&#x03C7;&#x03BF;&#x03BD;</term>,

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Bolus Armenus. </form> 
<xpln lang="en"><term lang="la">TErra, Lapis, Gleba</term>, or <term lang="la">Bolus Armenus</term>, after the sentence of
Galen, of colour pale. And c<expan type="">on</expan>cerning substance, moste
apte to be resolued into an equall smothnesse, as lime, and
is of a mightye dryinge power and therfore is precious for
the <term lang="la">Dysenteria</term>, the fluxe of the wombe, spittinge of bloude,
Catarhes, and putrefyinge vlcers of the mouthe. Howbeit
<expan type="">the</expan> kinde therof, which is commonly vsed in exterior grefes:
as it is muche more grosse, th<expan type="">en</expan> this here of Galen descri&#173;
bed, so is it in eche poynt, of muche lesse vertue, or efficacy. </xpln>

symplicium
medicamen. 
facultatibus. </term></note>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="ar">Bothor. </form> 
<xpln lang="en">THoughe this Arabye name <term lang="ar">Bothor</term>, be (after the mind
of diuers learned,) tak<expan type="">en</expan> for <term lang="la">Pustula</term> generally: yet is it
taken of Lanfrancus, Guido de Cauliaco, &#38;  others of <expan type="">the</expan> age
more streightly for a kynde of pustule, or exiture, growing
in <expan type="">the</expan> eye: which is of <term lang="ar">Iesu Hali</term>, thus described. <term lang="ar">Bothor</term> (saith he)
is a certeine eminence, or litle Aposteme, as they calle it, 
whyche c<expan type="">om</expan>meth of moysture, gathered betwene the rindes
of <term lang="la">Cornea</term>: wherof sayth he ther are. iiii. Galen in his defini&#173;
tions, calling it <term lang="gk">&#x03C3;&#x03C4;&#x03B1;&#x03C6;&#x03CD;&#x03BB;&#x03C9;&#x03BC;&#x03B1;</term>, (<term lang="la">id est Vua uel acinus Vua</term>) saith,
that it riseth in parte of the pupille, lyke the grayne of a
grape. And is made, when throughe peyne and inflamma&#173;



</page>

<page no="18">
tion, the pupille is reysed vp vpon highe, shewinge the figure,
of a graine of a grape, as afore. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Staphyloma. </term></note>
</wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Botium. </form> 
<xpln lang="en">ABoute this Aposteme, called in greke <term lang="gk">&#x03B2;&#x03C1;&#x03BF;&#x03B3;&#x03C7;&#x03BF;&#x03BA;&#x03AE;&#x03BB;&#x03B7;</term>,
<term lang="la">hoc est Tumor gutturis</term> Lanfrancus, and others aboute
that time, (thoughe they agree of his place,) do vary
in the substance, and mater therof. For Guido saythe, it is an
aposteme growinge oute of the necke, engendered of hu&#173;
mores, turned into euel mater. Brutus, and Theodoricus, saye
it is a fleshye aposteme, ingendered in the throte: Whyche
hapneth chiefly to women, and is of colour like their skin. 
and Lanfrancus in his greater worke, (agreing wel with ne&#173;
ther of them:) saith it is made of corrupt humores, &#38;  chiefly 
of Phlegme corrupted: But often of whot Apostemes, cor&#173;
rupted by longe retention of the mater, in the place affec&#173;
ted. Howe be it we oughte not to be astoned, at this varie&#173;
tye: since neyther of them, is therof a true description: But
rather doe seuerally serue, to seueral kindes therof. Which
are of <term lang="la">Celsus</term> seuerally described. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Bronchocele</term></note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Tumor guttu
ris</term></note>
</wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="brassica(n)">Brassica. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="cole(n)">IN Greke <term lang="gk">&#x039A;&#x1F78;&#x03AC;&#x03BC;&#x03B2;&#x03BD;</term>, is of . iii. kindes. <term lang="la">Esculenta</term>, <term lang="la">Agrestis</term>, &#38;  
<term lang="la">Marina</term>, but <term lang="la">Esculenta</term>, or <term lang="la">Satiua Brassica</term>, (which is our com&#173;
mon garden Cole,) is that whiche Lanfranke mentyo&#173;
neth: as well forbidding the vse therof, in the diet of those <expan type="">that</expan>
haue <term lang="la">Cancrum</term>, because it ingendereth grosse, and mel<expan type="">an</expan>cho&#173;
like iuyce:) as also teachinge proffitablye to vse the same, in
resolution. It is of temperamente whot and dry in the first
degre. It hathe by the testimonye of Galen dryinge power,
bothe eaten and outwardly applied, but is not very sharpe. 
It cureth <term lang="la">Erysipelata, Phlegmonnasque</term>, that are indurate and
harde to heale. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Crambe</term>. </note>
<lemenote>
The phrases "common garden cole", "garden cole", and "common cole" were not found in the OED. 
</lemenote>
</wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="bubo(n)">Bubo</form> 
<xpln lang="en"><term lang="gk">&#x0392;&#x03BF;&#x03C5;&#x03B2;&#x1F7C;&#x03BD;</term> (<term lang="la">id est tumor ing<damage>u</damage>in<damage>a</damage>rius</term>) <term lang="gk">&#x03A6;&#x03CD;&#x03BC;&#x03B1;</term>, <term lang="gk">&#x03A6;&#x03CD;&#x03B3;&#x03B5;&#x03B8;&#x03BB;&#x03BF;&#x03BD;</term>, Bubo, <term lang="gkt">Phy&#173;
ma</term>, and <term lang="gkt">Phygethlon</term>, saythe <term lang="la">Galenus</term>, are affectes of the Glan&#173; 



</page>

<page no="19">
dules. Bubo being only an inflammation of them. <term lang="gkt">Phyma</term>, is 
that whych forthwyth augmenteth, and hasteth to supura&#173;
tion. And <term lang="gkt">Phygethlon</term> is eyther <term lang="gkt">Erysipelas</term> in them wyth in&#173;
flammation or inflammati<expan type="">on</expan> wyth <term lang="gkt">Erysipelate</term>. But Guido (al&#173;
ledginge Auicenne in the end) taketh it three wayes thus. 
Firste saythe he, Bubo is properlye a sole Aposteme, lur&#173;
kinge in the arme holes, as dothe the Owle in the walles
of houses. Otherwise it is more larglye taken, for the Apo&#173;
steme, that ingendereth in anye of the emunctorye places. 
And thirdlye for all apostemes (generallye,) that growe in
glandulous m<expan type="">em</expan>bers. <term lang="la">Theodoricus</term> also defineth it to be a great
harde, and depe collection of mater, expelled from the prin&#173;
cipalle members, to the places aforesayde: wyth heate and
burning. But hereof in Lanfranke I finde no description. 
And note that as of Guido it may be gathered, this tumore
to haue thys name Bubo, or the Owle so called in Latine: so
is as well the herbe <term lang="la">Bubonem</term>
in the grindes,) called <term lang="la">Bubonium</term>, as also those partes it re&#173;
ceiuing <term lang="la">Bubones</term>. </xpln> 
<note type="m"><term lang="gk">Boubon</term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Libro. i. cap. i
de arte curati&#173;
ua, ad Glauco&#173;
nem. </term></note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Phyma</term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Phygethlon</term>. </note>

loke in myne

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Calx viua. </form> 
<xpln lang="en">OR lime unsl<emend err="">i</emend>cked: dothe vehementlye burne, and
Cauterize. But being utterly extincted, it remo&#173;
veth the eschare: and in processe of tyme, it wyll
make no eschare: although it beat and liquify the
flesh. And being often washed, it fryeth much, wythout bi&#173;
ting. It is a kinde of ashes, but of substance more subtil th<expan type="">en</expan>
the ashes of woode. The Grecians calle it <term lang="gk">&#x03C4;&#x03AF;&#x03C4;&#x03B1;&#x03BD;&#x03BF;&#x03BD;</term>. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Gale. de sym
wed. li. 8. &#38;. 9</term></note>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="cancer(n)">Cancer. </form> 
<xpln lang="en">OF the Aposteme Cancer, <emend err=")">(</emend> whiche the Grekes calle
<term lang="gk">&#x039A;&#x03B1;&#x03C1;&#x03BA;&#x03AF;&#x03BD;&#x03C9;&#x03BC;&#x03C2;</term>,) with hys causes, sygnes, and cure: hath
Lanfrancus so largely and sufficiently spoken, that
here nedeth no more therof be sayde. 



</page>

<page no="20">
but onlye to aduertise men of vnderstanding, rather to be&#173;
leue, not onlye Lanfranke, but also Galen: then by sole
hardinesse, (standinge to muche in theyr owne conceytes,)
to deceyue them selues and others, by takynge on them
thynges vncurable. 
<term lang="gk">&#x039A;&#x03B1;&#x03C1;&#x03BA;&#x1F76;&#x03BD;&#x03BF;&#x03C2;</term>, <term lang="la">id est Cancer fluuiatilis</term>. The river Crabbe, as it
is a specialle medicine against venim, and the hurts made
by virolente beastes: so is it of power to draw out thornes,
and slivers in the fleshe. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Carcinoma</term></note>
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Carcinos</term></note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Galenus de
Theriaca, ad
Pisonem</term>. </note>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cantharis</form> 
<xpln lang="en"><term lang="gk">&#x039A;&#x03B1;&#x03BD;&#x03B8;&#x03B1;&#x03C1;&#x03B9;&#x03C2;</term>, is a certeyne flye, of a grene colour. Which being
geuen wyth other mete diuretike medicines, dothe purge
the renes, and helpeth the difficulty of pissing: otherwise it
dothe as wel exulcerate the blader inwardly, as burne and
blister the skin, whersoeuer it be applied outwardly. </xpln>
<note type="m">Galenus, <term lang="la">libro
de theriaca ad
Pisonem</term>. </note>
</wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Caphura. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="camphor(n)">OF <term lang="la">Camphora</term>, there is a varietye of opinyon, because the
aunciente Grekes wryte not therof, neither anye
saue only the Arabians. For Platearius denieth it flat&#173;
lye to be the gum of a tree, affirminge it to be the iuyce of
an herbe, colde and drye in the fourthe degre. But Pandacta&#173;
rius and Antonius, Musa, Brasauolus, alledginge <term lang="la">Auicenn<expan type="">am</expan></term> and <term lang="la">Se&#173;
rapionem</term>, say it is the gum of a tree, or rather saythe Brasauo&#173;
lus, the pithe of the same, colde and drye in the third degre:
of a redde and spotty coloure. And is by sublimation (as by 
the heate of the sunne, or of fire,) made whyte, erre it come
to vs: takinge the name <term lang="ar">Camfor</term> amonge the Arabians, of
Panzor the place where it groweth. Or otherwyse, because 
it will hardlye be kepte. It coleth inflammat<emend err="t">i</emend>ons, stayeth
the fluxes of bloude, of the bellye, and of the eyes. And hea&#173;
leth whot vlcers, comforteth the senses, and taketh awaye
watchfulnesse. 



</page>

<page no="21">
And because it colynge (as before) in the third degre: yet
is easilye set on fyre, and yeldeth a cleare flame: and also be&#173;
cause nothinge is more odoriferous: Pandactarius moued be&#173;
like wyth the common principle, that euerye odoriferous
thinge is also whotte, accompted it a miracle: contrarye to
the minde of Galen, who iudgeth them to erre, that gesse
the faculties of medicynes by theyr odores. For neither is
euerye thinge whotte, (saythe he,) that smelleth well: nei&#173;
ther dothe euerye thing smell well, that is whotte. Ney&#173;
ther yet oughte any man to pronounce, euerye thinge that
stinketh coulde: nor euerye colde thinge, to haue a stync&#173;
kinge sauore. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="ar">Camfor</term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">De sym. med. 
fac. li. 2. cap. 3</term></note>
</wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cardamomum. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="cardamom(n)"><term lang="en">CArdamomum</term>, is of the later wryters distingued into ii. 
kyndes, <term lang="la">Maius</term> &#38;  <term lang="la">Minus</term>. Antonius Musa Brasauolus reco&#173;
neth . iii. sedes to be amonge the Apotheries vnder
that name extant, but neither of them as he also noteth, a&#173;
greeth wyth <term lang="la">Cardamomo Dioscoridis</term>, who havynge first she&#173;
wed from whence it is broughte, saythe thus. It ought to
be chosen whiche is fulle, fastened, and harde or toughe to
be broken, (for that whiche is not so is iudged olde,) sharpe
in taste and bitterish, whose odore greveth the head. With
thys saythe Brasauolus agreeth iustlye bothe in descriptyon
and facultyes <term lang="la">Cardumeni Serapionis</term>: but so doe none of the for&#173;
mer of the Apothecaryes, and therfore menne thinke we
have it not. Galenus measuringe the qualities of <term lang="la">Carda&#173;
momum</term>, wyth the temperamente of <term lang="la">Nasturtii</term> saythe, howe
muche the more swete, and fragrante it is, then <term lang="la">Nasturtio</term>. 
So muche the weaker is his facultye of heate: neyther is
it mete to ulcerate. yet hathe it therwyth adioyned a cer&#173;
taine bitternesse: wherby it killeth wormes, and with vi&#173;
neger, mundifieth scabbes strongly. Loke more for this in
<term lang="la">Grana paradisi</term>. </xpln>
<note type="m">Dioscorides. 
<term lang="la">libro. 1. </term></note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">libro. 7. de
symp. medi. 
facultatibus. </term></note>

<page no="22">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Carnes vari&#230;</form> 
<xpln lang="en">THe ingenderinge of fleshe, and what it is: you maye
reade in the nynthe Chapiter, of the first treatice, of
myne Anatomy. Fleshe (sayeth Galen,) Beinge well
sodde, maketh good bloude: namelye if it be fleshe of good
iuyce. Of al meates <term lang="la">caro suum</term> nourisheth moste. <term lang="la">bubula</term>
also giueth not a little nourishmente, but is harde to put o&#173;
uer, bredeth bloude to grosse, &#38; apt to cause mel<expan type="">an</expan>cholike, af&#173;
fected. And, as to yong men in good habite of body, the flesh
of a grown hogge, is better than a pigge: so is veale better
than beffe, and kiddes flesh better than gotes fleshe: whych
are muche better &#38; easier concocted. Lambes fleshe is very
moist &#38;  Phlegmaticke: but mutton maketh more iuyce, and more
excrementes. The gotes flesh hath a sharpe &#38; vicious
iuyce. Kiddes fleshe is not euel for old persons. <term lang="la">Caro hircorum</term>
is both of iuyce and concoction the worst. The like may be
sayde of beffe or rammes fleshe: but of all these the gelded
are the better: as the olde fleshe is worse. Hares fleshe bre&#173;
deth grosse bloud, but better iuyce then beffe. Hartes flesh
or buckes flesh, is hard to concoct. And make as euel iuyce 
as any of the rest: &#38; therfore are Hartes flesh, Gotes fleshe
and beffe, profitable neither for old nor yong. To y<expan type="">on</expan>g men
mutton is admitted, though to old men it be not commodi&#173;
ous: and muche lesse lambes fleshe. 
Euery kinde of flying foule, geueth very litle nourysh&#173;
ment, in respect of beastes. The fleshe of foules is easye to
concoct, chiefly of <expan type="">the</expan> bird called <term lang="la">Attagen</term>, (which some thinke
is the woodcoke. ) The fleshe of the blacke bird, the owsel &#38;
the smal sparowes, are harder: but harder then they, is the
flesh of the turtle doue, the wood doue, &#38;  the ducke. But to
conclude. <term lang="la">Cum Cibis etiam animalium mutantur carnes</term>. That is <expan type="">the</expan> 
flesh of beastes &#38;  fowles are altered, by theyr feding. And 
therfore are the birdes alowed, that are conuersant on the
swete billes, in the holesome grauelly woodes, and plesant
groues: as suche as liue in marishes, or fennes, and fede in
the water, are vtterly escheued. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">De alimentis. 
li. iii. </term></note>
<note type="m">Hogges flesh</note>
<note type="m">Beefe. </note>
<note type="m">The he gotes
fleshe. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">De sanitate
t<damage>ue</damage>nda. li. 5. </term></note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">De sym. li. ii. </term></note>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="causon(n)">Causon. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="ardent(a)" lexeme="fever(n)"><term lang="gk">&#x039A;&#x03AC;&#x03C5;&#x03C3;<expan type="">&#x03BF;&#x03C2;</expan></term>, <term lang="la">id est febris ardens</term>: is one of the continuall feuers,
and hath to name <term lang="la">tertians continua</term>: caused of yelow choler,
putrefied in the veines, (none otherwise then <term lang="la">Quotidians c<expan type="">on</expan>&#173;
tinua</term>, commeth of putrefied phlegme and <term lang="la">Quartans c<expan type="">on</expan>tinua</term> of
corrupted melancholy,) and differeth from <term lang="la">Tertiani intermit&#173;
tente</term>, for that therin the cholericke humor is caried over all
the body. But in Ardente febre, it is together with the bloud,
conteined in the vessels: causyng muche payne &#38; burnyng. 
Whervnto (saith Galen,) if rigor at any tyme chaunce: the
Feuer is therby disolued. 
Yet some neuerthelesse, make a certain obscure differ<expan type="">en</expan>s
betwene Causon &#38;  <term lang="gkt">Synocho</term>,) and that rather of the colde t<expan type="">em</expan>perature
of that tyme, then of hys owne nature. </xpln>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la" lexeme="cassia(n)">Casia. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="cinnamon(n)"><term lang="la">Casia Fistularis</term>, or <term lang="la">Cassis syringa</term>, is (by the testimony of A&#173;
uicen and Mesues,) meane betwene whotte and colde. 
But inclining rather, to heat and moisture in <expan type="">the</expan> first
degree. it is the frute of a tre, brought forth in hard blacke
coddes. Wholse inwarde pulpe, is resolutiue, and lenityue,
clenseth the blood and purgeth g<expan type="">en</expan>tly Choler &#38;  Phlegme. 
And thys out of the Arabians, for amonge the old Greci<expan type="">an</expan>s
it is not found: who yet haue their <term lang="la">Cassion fistularem</term>, whych
is of some taken for oure Cinamome. </xpln>
</wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cepa. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="onion(n)" lexeme="sive(n)" lexeme="winter onion(n)" lexeme="holleke(n)">CAlled in greke <term lang="gk">&#x039A;&#x03C1;&#x03CC;&#x03BC;&#x03BC;&#x03C5;&#x03BF;&#x03BD;</term>, is of diuers kindes, as this

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chelidonium. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="celandine(n)" lexeme="swallowwort(n)" lexeme="pilewort(n)">CAlled in Englishe Salendine, or Swallow Wurte,
in Greke <term lang="gk">&#x03C7;&#x03B5;&#x03BB;&#x03B9;&#x03BF;&#x03C5;&#x03CC;&#x03BD;&#x03B9;&#x03BF;&#x03BD;</term>, <term lang="la">hoc est Hirundinaria</term>, (so called ei&#173;
ther because it bloweth, aboute the returne of swal&#173;
lowes in the spring, and wythereth agayne at their depar&#173;
ture: or else as Plinius wryteth, because the Swallowes did
fyrste fynde and use the same, so restore again their birdes
to syghte, beinge made blinde:) is of heatinge, and scou&#173;
ringe propertyes. His roote is giuen (<term lang="la">in Vino albo cum aniso</term>,)
to the Iaundies that come of the liuer obstructed: and be&#173;
inge chawed, helpeth the tothake. The iuyce of the herbe
is used in the eye, to sharpen the syght. And thus muche of
<term lang="la">Chelidonium Maius</term>. For ther is also <term lang="la">Chelidonium Minus</term>: which
(as it is sharper than the greater,) doth swiftly exulcerate. 
And the iuyce therof purgeth the head by the nosethrilles. 
It heateth and byndeth in the beginninge of the fourthe de&#173;
gree, the greater onlye in the thirde. Wherfore that the
herbe called of the Latin wryters and apothecaries <term lang="la">Ficaria,
&#38; Scrofularia minor</term>, in Englishe Pyle worte, (whose Picture
is vsually put, and not of the worste Herbal wryters
for this:) is not <term lang="la">Chelidonium Minus</term>, it is evident. Whose tem&#173;
peramentes, (though the description of <term lang="la">Chelidonium</term> in <term lang="la">Dios&#173;
coride</term> will suffer it in forme to agree:) are one to an other
cleane contraries. </xpln>

de sym. medi. 
facultatibus. </term></note>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="surgery(n)">Chirurgery. </form> 
<xpln lang="en"><term lang="gk">&#x03A7;&#x03B5;&#x03B9;&#x03C1;&#x03BF;&#x03C1;&#x03B3;&#x03B9;&#x03B1;</term> is sayd of euery arte, whose function consisteth,
in manualle action or handye operation. But here it is to

<page no="26">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cicatrizatiua med. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="cicatrix(n)">CIcatrix is the scarre or token, where a wounde, vl&#173;
cer &#38;c. hathe bene, Wherof commeth Cicatrizo, <term lang="la">id est
ad Cicatricem perduco</term>, to heale or brynge to a skarre. 
And therof riseth <term lang="la">Medicamina cicatrizatius</term>, Cicatrisinge, con&#173;
founding, or skin bringing medicynes. </xpln>
</wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="cicer(n)">Cicer. </form> 
<xpln lang="en">IS a flatuous pulse, of greate nourishment, mouynge the
wombe, apte to ingender mylke, and to prouoke vrine
&#38; Menses. Called in Greke <term lang="gk">&#x0395;&#x03C1;&#x03B5;&#x03B2;&#x03B9;&#x03BD;&#x03B8;<expan type="">&#x03BF;&#x03C2;</expan></term>. and is after Di&#173;
oscorides of . iii. kyndes: namelye <term lang="la">Satiuum</term>, wherof afore. <term lang="la">Areti&#173;
num</term>, whose decoction breaketh <expan type="">the</expan> stone in the reines. (which 
is also of . iii. sortes,) and <term lang="la">Syluestre</term>. They are all whotte, mo&#173;
deratlye drye, and partners of bitternesse. Wherby they
purge the splene, the liuer, and the reines. They mundifye
scabbes, and lepryes. They also discusse the hardnesse of <expan type="">the</expan>
stones, and Apostemes vnder the eares, and doe heale in
composition, maligne vlcers. Thoughe a <term lang="la">Domestico</term>: as it is
(then it) sharper, and bitterer. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Erebinthos</term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Diosco. lib. ii. </term></note>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="cichorium(n)">Cichorium. </form> 
<xpln lang="en">IT is playne by Dioscorides and others, that thys Greke
worde <term lang="gk">&#x03C3;&#x03AD;&#x03C1;&#x03B9;&#x03C3;</term>, is a name common and indifferente, bothe
to Cichorium, (whyche is also called <term lang="gk">&#x03C0;&#x03B9;&#x03BA;&#x03C1;&#x03B9;&#x03C2;</term>,) and to <term lang="la">Intubum</term>,
wyth also al theyr kindes. They are cold, somwhat bitter,
and moderatly astringente: and therfore moste comodious
for the stomacke, and conueniente in chiefe for the heat of
the liuer. Being eaten wyth vineger, they stay the belly. 
<term lang="la">Intubum domesticum</term> is colder than Agreste, whiche is cold and
drye in the seconde degre, and bitterer then the tame, (and 
is surelye the righte Cichorium,) and therefore not at eache
poynte so commodious to the stomache. They are (in <term lang="la">Cata&#173;
plasmatibus</term>,) good medicynes for the gowte of the feete, and
the inflammations of the eyes. Theyr iuyces <term lang="la">cum Cerussa,



</page>

<page no="27">
&#38; aceto</term>, are for all griefes profitable, that nede coling. And
yet that dothe it so moderatly, that euen to colde distempe&#173;
ratures it hurteth not. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Seris</term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Picris</term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Dioscori. li. 2
cum Galeno
li. 8. de symp. 
medi. faculta&#173;

de compositi&#173;
one medicam<expan type="">en</expan><emend err="">&#173;</emend>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Colla de corio. </form> 
<xpln lang="en">LAnfranke meaneth heare by <term lang="la">Colla de Corio</term>, that glewe
that some (saythe Dioscorides) caule <term lang="gk">&#x03C5;&#x03BB;&#x03cc;&#x03BA;&#x03BF;&#x03BB;&#x03BB;&#x03B1;&#x03BD;</term>, and o&#173;
thers <term lang="gk">&#x03BE;&#x03C4;&#x03B1;&#x03CC;&#x1F78;&#x1f78;&#x03BA;&#x03BF;&#x03BB;&#x03BB;&#x03B1;&#x03BD;</term>, <term lang="la">hoc est Glut<expan type="">en</expan>, Vel Glutinum taurinum</term>,
made of Bullockes hydes. The best is whyte, and shinyng
throughe, but the blacker it is, the worse. It resolued in <term lang="la">A&#173;
ceto</term>, deliuereth the skin of ring wormes, and lepyres. Bur&#173;
ned blisters, are by washynge them in the decoction therof
kept from breaking. And <term lang="la">Cum Melle aut aceto</term>, It is pro&#173;
fitable for woundes, and confoundeth them. 
And as thys beinge made of the skinnes and eares of
dyuers beastes, is of diuers sortes, and maye so varye in
name: so is there glewe made of diuers sortes of Fyshes,
whych is generally called <term lang="gk">&#x03B9;&#x03C7;&#x03B4;&#x03C5;&#x03BF;&#x03BA;&#x03BF;&#x03BB;&#x03BB;&#x03B1;</term>, and may in names
particularly vary as the other. 
They haue all drying faculty, but doe vary in heatynge
and cooling, as the substances wherof they are made. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Xylocoll<expan type="">an</expan></term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Taurocolla</term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Gluten,
Glutinum tau<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
rinum</term></note>
</wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="colocynth(n)">Colocynthis. </form> 
<xpln lang="en"><term lang="gk">&#x039A;&#x03BF;&#x03BB;&#x03BF;&#x03BA;&#x03CD;&#x03BD;&#x03B4;&#x03B9;&#x03C2;</term>, called in Latine <term lang="la">Cucurbita Syluestris</term>, and of the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Contusio. </form>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Consolidatiue&#230; medicin&#230;</form> 
<xpln lang="en">COnsolidatyue medicynes, of <term lang="la">Consolido</term>, to make fyrme
and sounde. Lanfranke sayth, that they are all one with
Cicatrizatiues, because theyr effectes doe so well ac&#173;
corde, in finishyng the cure of woundes, vlcers, fistules, &#38;c. 
whyche saythe Galen they doe not by drawing and liquy&#173;
fyinge the fleshe: but by hardeninge and dryinge the same. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">De symp, li. 5</term></note>
</wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Corallium. </form> 
<xpln lang="en">WHiche some haue called <term lang="gk"> &#x039B;&#x03AF;&#x03B8;&#x03BF;&#x03B4;&#x03AD;&#x03BD;&#x03B4;&#x03C1;&#x03BF;&#x03BD;</term>, semeth (sayth Di&#173;
oscorides) to be a shrubbe of the sea, which being drawn
oute from the depthe: as sone as it commeth into the aer,
dothe by and by congeyle and harden. It groweth in Syra&#173;
cusa, about the Promontory Pachyno. It is of diuers colours,
(other saye kindes,) wherof the redde is the best. It coleth
and bindeth moderatly, it taketh awaye the scarres of the 
eyes, and filleth holowe vlcers and woundes. It is agaynst
reiections of bloude, verye efficacious and helpeth the dif&#173;
ficultye of vrine: drunke also wyth water, it wasteth the
splene. The blacke coralle (which resembleth a bushy tre,)
called <term lang="gk">&#x1F00;&#x03BD;&#x03C4;&#x03B9;&#x03C0;&#x03B1;&#x03B8;&#x1F74;&#x03C2;</term>, agreeth in vertues wyth the former, and
is thought to differ only in <term lang="la">Specie</term>. </xpln>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Corrigiola. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="corrigiole(n)" lexeme="knot-grass(n)">SO called of the Apothecaries, and of the Frenche men
<term lang="fr">Corrigiole</term>, is oure common knottgrasse, called in Greke
<term lang="gk">&#x03C0;&#x03BF;&#x03BB;&#x03CD;&#x03B3;&#x03BF;&#x03BD;&#x03BF;&#x03BD;</term>, in Latine <term lang="la">Seminalis</term>, and <term lang="la">Polygonum mas</term>. For

Galen make onlye two kindes, as <term lang="la">Mas</term> &#38;  <term lang="la">Femina</term>. Thoughe
Plinius and other later wryters haue moe. <term lang="la">P<emend err="ylo">oly</emend>gonum</term> after

seconde excesse, or in the beginninge of the third: And ther&#173;
fore beinge applied colde, is a remedye for whotte burning
stomaches, for the tumor <term lang="la">Erysipelas</term>, and whotte inflamma&#173;
tions. And farther it stayeth all fluxions, by the which rea&#173;
son it semeth to haue drying power, and therfore is a good 
remedy to Vlcers, and Teters, and glueth together blou&#173;
dy woundes. But the male sayth he (aledginge Dioscorides,)
is in all these the more potente. </xpln>

<xpln lang="en" lexeme="quince tree(n)" lexeme="quince(n)"><term lang="la">COtonea malus</term>, in Greke <term lang="la">&#x039A;&#x03C5;&#x03B4;&#x03C0;&#x03BD;&#x03B9;&#x03BF;&#x03B6; &#x03BC;&#x03B5;&#x03BB;&#x03B5;&#x03AC;</term> is the Quince

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="cotyledon(n)">Cotyledon. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="pennywort(n)"><term lang="la">VMbilicus Veneris</term>, (called in Greke <term lang="gk">&#x039A;&#x03B1;&#x03C4;&#x03C5;&#x03BB;&#x03B7;&#x03B4;&#x1F7C;&#x03BD;</term>, in La&#173;
tine of some <term lang="la">Acetabulum</term>, and in Englishe Penyworte.)
Is coulde of temperamente, somwhat moyste, and fulle of
iuyce. It groweth on stone walles, and hathe after Galen,
a light bitternes, and also a certayne obscure adstringente
facultye. Wherby it dothe coole, repercusse, scoure away,
and discusse. And therfore healeth wel Erisipelatous infl<expan type="">am</expan>&#173;
mations, &#38; Phlegmonus <term lang="la">Erisipelata</term>, and is to a whotte sto&#173;
mache in a <term lang="la">Cataplasma</term> most commodious. An other kinde
of this herbe ther is growinge in marishes, whyche is cal&#173;
led <term lang="la">Cotyledon Aquaticum</term>, and is of nature very whotte, lyke
to the whotted kindes of <term lang="la">Ramunculus</term>. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Acetabulum</term>. </note>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="crocus(n)">Crocus</form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="saffron(n)">SAffron called in Greke <term lang="gk">&#x039A;&#x03C1;&#x03CC;&#x03BA;<expan type="">&#x03BF;&#x03C2;</expan></term>, dothe heate in the se&#173;
conde degree, and drye in the first. Wherof the yelow&#173;

mores, and virulent affects. It moueth vrine and maketh
a good coloure. beinge drunke <term lang="la">cum Passo</term>, it defendeth surfe&#173;
tynge: and applied wyth womans milke, restraineth the
fluxions of the eyes. Howe be it the continualle vse therof,
and the smelling therto, hurteth the head. </xpln>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="cubeb(n)">Cubebe. </form> 
<xpln lang="en">THe thin odoriferous frutes, (tasted like the rootes of 
Phu,) whiche the Arabians calle <term lang="ar">Cubebas</term>: is that which
Galen calleth <term lang="la">Carpesium</term>, as Auicen, Aetius, Actuarius, &#38;  
Ruellius, wryte, (whiche yet Leonicenus denieth, and others
make therof a doubte. ) And is saythe Serapio, the frute of a
tree, growinge beyonde the seas, whose leaues are sharpe
lyke a speare. The frute is found among the leaues, round 



</page>

<page no="31">
and somwhat flat. Whi<damage>c</damage>he when it is ripe, is of coloure re&#173;
dishe. Wherin is found a trianguled grain. But this is by 
the iudgemente of Antonius Musa, the description of <term lang="la">Myrtus
Syluestris</term>, and the frutes of the same dothe Serapio call <term lang="ar">Cube&#173;
bas</term>, whiche differ from our vulgar <term lang="la">Cucubis</term>. <term lang="la">Carpesium</term>, saithe
Galen is like to Valerian, bothe in taste and facultyes, but
hathe more subtiltye, and therefore clenseth, and scoureth
more, the obstructions of the bowels, moueth vryne, and
purgeth the renes, pained wyth stones. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Galenus de
simplici. lib. 7</term></note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Carpesium</term>. </note>
</wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cucumis asminus. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="cucumber(n)">THoughe ther be diuers kindes of Cucumers, (&#38; they
not wythout their singuler, &#38;  eximious vertues:) we
haue here only to speake of the wilde, or leaping Cu&#173;
cumer, called <term lang="gk">&#x03C3;&#x03AF;&#x03BA;&#x03C5;&#x03C2; &#x03AC;&#x03B3;&#x03C1;&#x03B9;<expan type="">&#x03BF;&#x03C2;</expan></term>, &#38;  of the Apothecaries <term lang="la">Cucumis
asminus</term>. It is very bitter, and beinge layde to wyth Barlye
floure, breaketh every old coughe. The iuyce of the leaues,
instilled into the eares, helpeth they paines: and being ap&#173;
plies with Terebinthin resin, it breaketh smal Apostemes. 
It easeth also the gowte, the tothe ache, &#38;  the <term lang="la">Ischiada</term> paine. 
The roote therof is of abstersiue and mollificatyue facul&#173;
tyes. The iuyce wherof and the rynde, (which drieth more
strongly,) geuen together doe purge Choler and Phlegme
chiefly in <term lang="la">Hydropicis</term>, and putteth forth deiections, wythout
hurting the stomacke. 

Out of the frute saith Dioscorides, is prepared a iuyce, (or
else pressed out of the rotes &#38;  leaues saith Galen,) called <term lang="la">Ela&#173;
terium</term>: whot in the seconde degree, and meruailous bytter. 
And therfore digesteth, moueth vryne, and healeth paynes
of the head. And finallye it dothe all, that the herbe, rote or
frute doeth, and that more strongly. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Sicys Agrios</term>. </note>
<note type="m">Dioscorides
<term lang="la">li. 4. &#38;  Gal&#173;
nus, li. 8. de
sym. med. fa&#173;
cultatibus. </term></note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Elaterium</term>. </note>
</wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cucurbita. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="gourd(n)">Called in greke <term lang="gk">&#x039A;&#x03BF;&#x03BB;&#x03CC;&#x03BA;&#x03B9;&#x03BD;&#x03B8;&#x03B1;</term>, is a frute apt to be eat<expan type="">en</expan> raw,
and is of diuers sortes, differing rather in forme then in fa&#173;

</page>

The slyces or peeces therof, are layde to the nodle of chil&#173;
dren, againste the vehemente heate of theyr heades, called
<term lang="la">Syriasis</term>. They coole also the inflammations of the eyes, and
the gowte of the fete: and do helpe moreouer, the adustion
of the skin, and the vehement heat of feuers. The iuyce al&#173;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cupressus. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="cypress(n)">CIpresse is a tree called in Greeke <term lang="gk">&#x039A;&#x03C5;&#x03C0;&#x03AC;&#x03C1;&#x03B9;&#x03C3;&#x03C3;&#x03BF;&#x03C2;</term>, in La&#173;
tyne <term lang="la">Cupressus</term>, and of the Apothecaries <term lang="la">Cypressius</term>. It
cooleth and dryeth as Dioscorides saythe, <term lang="la">Libro. 1. </term>. The
leaues and nuttes therof , are used for those purposes in
medicynes. The leaues, braunches, and y<expan type="">on</expan>g tender nuttes
of Cypres doe drye (saythe Galen) wythout great sharpnes
or heate, and heale greate ulcers in harde bodies. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Cyparisses</term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">De sympli. 7. </term></note>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="curcuma(n)">Curcuma. </form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="madder(n)" lexeme="saffron(n)">AS saythe Syluius vpon <term lang="la">Mesuen</term>, is that wyth the Ara&#173;
bian<emend err=",s">s,</emend> whiche the Grecians calle <term lang="gk">&#x0395;&#x03C1;&#x03C5;&#x03B8;&#x03C1;&#x03CC;&#x03B4;&#x03B1;&#x03BD;&#x03BF;&#x03BD;</term>, the
Latines <term lang="la">Rubiam</term> and <term lang="la">Rubeam tinctorum</term>, and we Ma&#173;
der: Thoughe some applye that name to Chelidonio, and o&#173;
thers corruptly to Saffron. And as this hys assertion hath
manye learned fautores, and therfore seemeth moste true:
so is it verye lyke to be that whiche Lanfranke meaneth,
for that it agreeth with his purpose, (Who putteth it a&#173;
monge his consolidatiues,) whiche the other doe not. 
The roote of <term lang="la">Rubia</term> is sharpe, and bitter: and therfore ex&#173;
purgeth the Liuer &#38; the splene: Prouoketh muche grosse,
and sometime bloudye vrines, and scoureth meanlye. And
therfore helpeth <term lang="la">Ischiada</term> payne also, and loosed members. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Erythrodan<expan type="">on</expan></term>. </note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Rubia. </term></note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Galenus de 
sym. li. 6. </term></note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Diosco. lib. 3. </term></note>
<lemenote>
"Curcuma" antedates the earliest OED citation (1617). 
</lemenote>
</wordentry>
</wordgroup1>

<xpln lang="en">DEfensiue medicynes (of <term lang="la">Defendo</term> to guarde, defend
and prohibite. ) Are of no smalle profite to the
Chirurgien hys worke, whose vse and vtilityes



</page>

<page no="33">
may by the circumstances (where so euer they are mencio&#173;
ned) be easily gathered. </xpln>

serue often the office of Cicatrizatiues, loke there. </xpln>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dipsacum. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="teasel(n)"><term lang="la">DIpsacum</term> called also <term lang="la">Labrum Veneris</term>, and of the Apothe&#173;
caries <term lang="la">Carduus Fullonum</term>, is called in Greke <term lang="gk">&#x03B4;&#x03AF;&#x03C8;&#x03B1;&#x03BA;&#x03BF;&#x03C3;</term>
and in Englishe Teasell. Ther are two kindes ther
of. The one the shermen occupye: The other whiche is cal&#173;
led <term lang="la">Dipsacum album</term>, serueth after the minde of some,) chiefly 
for medicines. 

<term lang="la">Radix dipsaci</term> (saythe Galen) dryeth in the seconde degree,
and hathe not a little abstersion. It healeth (by the testimo&#173;
ny of Dioscorides,) fistules, and chappes of the fundamente,
beinge brused and boyled wyth wyne, til it be as thycke as
were. And further is thoughte to be a remedye, for ryng-
wormes, and hanginge wartes. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">Labrum Ve&#173;
neris</term>. </note>

sym. li. 6. </term></note>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="dyscrasy(n)">Dyscrasia. </form> 
<xpln lang="en"><term lang="gk">&#x03B4;&#x03C5;&#x03C3;&#x03BA;&#x03B1;&#x03C3;&#x03AF;&#x03B1;</term> <term lang="la">id est Intemperics</term>, (that is distemperance) is after
Galen <term lang="la">Aequalis</term>, which is wythout payne, because ther is in
the place affected, a desired nature, (for no bodye is by hys
owne nature infested) or <term lang="la">Inaqualis</term>, whiche is when a bo&#173;
dye is troubled bothe wyth heate and cold at once, or with
drinesse and moisture, more then to nature is conuenient. 
Which sometymes chaunceth, though it seeme vnlyke:
and how greate so euer it be, so muche dothe it moleste. 
These are eighte in number, and may seuerally chance, to 
the eyghte symple members: requiringe also, so manye dif&#173;
ferences of curation. And are eyther symple, whyche maye
be . iiii. wayes, whot, cold, dry, or moiste, and maye be cured 
by theyr contraries: or compound as many wayes, as whot



</page>

<page no="34">

and drye, whotte and moyste. &#38;c. With these dispositions
one part, or moe, or the whole body may be affected. 
</xpln>

matum causis
li. 2. </term></note>
<note type="m"><term lang="la">De methodo
medenci,li. 7. 
8. &#38;. 9. . </term></note>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="ephemera(n)">Ephemera. </form> 
<xpln lang="en">WHyche (by changing . &#x03BA;. into . &#x03AF;:) hathe accustomablye
bene wryten <term lang="la">Ephimera</term>: Is a feuer happeninge chieflye
to melancholike persons, thoughe sometime it chaunce of
rawnesse, to bilious temperamentes: springinge of a pro&#173;
catarctike cause, (which is therof an inseparable token, yet
therto not proper:) as weariness, drunkennesse, wrathe,
furye, sorowe, and suche other vehement affectes of the 
minde: and sometyme of bloude inflamed, or of the tumor
Bubo: contynueth wyth a swete or pleasant heate, and incly&#173;
neth wyth some swete dewe or good vapor: after <expan type="">the</expan> whiche
commeth healthe. The naturalle tyme of continuance, is
one naturalle daye: wherin it is apte to be resolued, and
therfore is called <term lang="la">Febris diaria</term>, and in Greke <term lang="gk">&#x0395;&#x03C6;&#x1F75;&#x03BC;&#x03B5;&#x03C1;&#x03B1; 
&#x03BA;&#x03B1;&#x03B9;
&#x03C0;&#x03C5;&#x03C1;&#x03B5;&#x03C4;&#x03BF;&#x03C3; &#x1F10;&#x03C6;&#x03AE;&#x03BC;&#x03B5;&#x03C1;&#x03BF;&#x03C3;</term>. But thys end it taketh, by good gover&#173;
nance in the beginninge: which if it passe, it sometyme
changeth bothe name and nature, and sometime only the
name referrynge the nature. And this state of <term lang="la">Ephemera</term> I
iudge Lanfranke to meane where he speaketh of <term lang="la">Ephemera
continua</term>. </xpln>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="euphorbium(n)">Euphorbium</form> 
<xpln lang="en"><term lang="gk">&#x0395;&#x03C5;&#x03C6;&#x03CC;&#x03C1;&#x03B2;&#x03B9;&#x03BF;&#x03B7;</term>: is the gum or teares of a tree, called Euphorbia,
growinge in Lybia, found out (by the testimonye of Dioscori&#173;
des,) in <expan type="">the</expan> time of Iuba: and was called by that name, (as saith 
Ruellius,) of his Phisicien. It hath a vehemente whotte, and
burninge facultye, and profiteth verye muche againste the
Spasme, caused by the pricking of tendones. But for that 
oughte it not to be vsed to newe, (which is of colour cleare
whyte,) for the vehemente heate therof: Neyther to olde,
(which then waxeth yelow or pale,) because it is numbred
among suche symples, as doe soone lose theyr heat and ver&#173;
tues. And yet continueth it . vi. yeres. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Euphorbion</term>. </note>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Faba. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="bean(n)">CAlled in Greke <term lang="gk">&#x039A;&#x03C5;&#x03B1;&#x03BC;<expan type="0+sigma">&#x03BF;&#x03C2;</expan></term> coleth &#38; drieth meane&#173;
lye. Yet hathe the meale therof, some abstertion,
as also the hulles haue not a litle adstringente fa&#173;
cultye. To be eaten they are flatul<expan type="">en</expan>t, though they
be neuer so muche sodden: harde to be concocted, and cause
spittinges out of the brest &#38; lunges: but they nurish much. 
In medicynes outwardlye, they drye vnhurtfully: and be&#173;
inge boyled in water, were often vsed of Galen, <term lang="la">cum adipi
suillo</term>, to the goutes of the fete. The meale is incarnatyue,
and is put to bruses, and in wounds of sinewes, <term lang="la">cum Oximi&#173;
lite</term>, and to inflammations <term lang="la">cum Polenta</term>. And is in <term lang="la">Cataplasma&#173;
tis</term> moste apte, for swellinges of the pappes and stones. 
And although many learned men, by diuers reas<expan type="">on</expan>s (which
I omitte) moued of late, doe doubte whether oure Beane
maye be taken for <term lang="la">Faba</term>, or for <term lang="la">Phasiolo</term>, or otherwyse howe:
Yet nede no man doubt (in my iudgement) that Lanfranke
as well as many other wryters bothe before him, and long 
tyme since haue for <term lang="la">Faba</term> vnderstanded the Beane. </xpln>
<note type="m"><term lang="gkt">Cyamos</term>. </note>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fabaria. </form> 
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="orpine(n)" lexeme="lempke(n)" lexeme="brooklime(n)" lexeme="worm-grass(n)" lexeme="sedum(n)">THat whiche the Italians calle <term lang="it">Fabariam</term>, is thought of 
some to be <term lang="la">Telephium</term>, and called of others <term lang="gkt">Cymbalion</term>,
but neyther of bothe trulye. The later wryters calle
it <term lang="la">Crassulam maorent, Lacobus Mantius</term> wyth dyuers other, <term lang="la">Fa&#173;
bam grossam</term>, we (and also the French men,) cal it Orpin, and 
aunciently Lempke. whervnto some haue added, (as a kind
therof,) the herbe that D. Turner, thinketh to be <term lang="la">Capea</term> of 
Dioscorides, calling it <term lang="la">Fabaria minor</term>, or <term lang="la">Fabaria aquatica</term>, and eng&#173;
lishly brooke Lempke. But <term lang="la">Crassula minor</term>, is *by the comm<expan type="">on</expan>
consente, of almoste all the learned,) that kind of stone



</page>

<page no="37">
croppe, that groweth comm<expan type="">on</expan>ly upon stone walles or hou&#173;
ses, as Sedum dothe, hauinge round blunte leaues, like pud&#173;
dinges or litle wormes, ful of iuyce, called also of the forme
aforsayde, <term lang="la">Vermicularis</term>, in Englishe Wormegrasse: wherof
more at <term lang="la">Semper Viuum</term>. 
The later wryters, (for the olde make therof no menci&#173;
on,) doe praise theyr <term lang="la">Crassulam maiorem</term>, for the greate efficacy
that it hathe, in curynge woundes, in stoppynge of bloude,
chieflye for inwarde woundes and ulcers: and for the mer&#173;
uailous profit it giveth, in healinge ruptures. </xpln>
